###begin article-title 0
###xml 108 130 108 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Legionella pneumophila</italic>
###xml 108 130 <span type="species:ncbi:446">Legionella pneumophila</span>
Identification of Host Cytosolic Sensors and Bacterial Factors Regulating the Type I Interferon Response to Legionella pneumophila
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Conceived and designed the experiments: KMM SMM REV. Performed the experiments: KMM SMM REV. Analyzed the data: KMM SMM REV. Contributed reagents/materials/analysis tools: KMM SMM. Wrote the paper: KMM SMM REV.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 0 22 0 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Legionella pneumophila</italic>
###xml 187 201 187 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 357 371 357 371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 422 436 422 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 697 711 697 711 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 791 805 791 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 872 886 872 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1018 1032 1018 1032 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1138 1152 1138 1152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 0 22 <span type="species:ncbi:446">Legionella pneumophila</span>
###xml 187 201 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 357 371 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 422 436 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 697 711 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 791 805 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 872 886 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1018 1032 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1138 1152 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Legionella pneumophila is a gram-negative bacterial pathogen that replicates in host macrophages and causes a severe pneumonia called Legionnaires' Disease. The innate immune response to L. pneumophila remains poorly understood. Here we focused on identifying host and bacterial factors involved in the production of type I interferons (IFN) in response to L. pneumophila. It was previously suggested that the delivery of L. pneumophila DNA to the host cell cytosol is the primary signal that induces the type I IFN response. However, our data are not easily reconciled with this model. We provide genetic evidence that two RNA-sensing proteins, RIG-I and MDA5, participate in the IFN response to L. pneumophila. Importantly, these sensors do not seem to be required for the IFN response to L. pneumophila DNA, whereas we found that RIG-I was required for the response to L. pneumophila RNA. Thus, we hypothesize that bacterial RNA, or perhaps an induced host RNA, is the primary stimulus inducing the IFN response to L. pneumophila. Our study also identified a secreted effector protein, SdhA, as a key suppressor of the IFN response to L. pneumophila. Although viral suppressors of cytosolic RNA-sensing pathways have been previously identified, analogous bacterial factors have not been described. Thus, our results provide new insights into the molecular mechanisms by which an intracellular bacterial pathogen activates and also represses innate immune responses.
###end p 2
###begin title 3
Author Summary
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 420 442 420 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Legionella pneumophila</italic>
###xml 626 640 626 640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 687 701 687 701 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 752 766 752 766 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 969 983 969 983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 420 442 <span type="species:ncbi:446">Legionella pneumophila</span>
###xml 626 640 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 687 701 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 752 766 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 969 983 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Initial detection of invading microorganisms is one of the primary tasks of the innate immune system. However, the molecular mechanisms by which pathogens are recognized remain incompletely understood. Here, we provide evidence that an immunosurveillance pathway (called the RIG-I/MDA5 pathway), thought primarily to detect viruses, is also involved in the innate immune response to an intracellular bacterial pathogen, Legionella pneumophila. In the response to viruses, the RIG-I/MDA5 immunosurveillance pathway has been shown to respond to viral RNA or DNA. We found that the RIG-I pathway was required for the response to L. pneumophila RNA, but was not required for the response to L. pneumophila DNA. Thus, one explanation of our results is that L. pneumophila RNA may access the host cell cytosol, where it triggers the RIG-I/MDA5 pathway. This is unexpected since bacteria have not previously been thought to translocate RNA into host cells. We also found that L. pneumophila encodes a secreted bacterial protein, SdhA, which suppresses the RIG-I/MDA5 pathway. Several viral repressors of the RIG-I/MDA5 pathway have been described, but bacterial repressors of RIG-I/MDA5 are not known. Thus, our study provides novel insights into the molecular mechanisms by which the immune system detects bacterial infection, and conversely, by which bacteria suppress innate immune responses.
###end p 4
###begin title 5
Introduction
###end title 5
###begin p 6
###xml 28 50 28 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Legionella pneumophila</italic>
###xml 125 139 125 139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 245 248 245 248 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Fields1">[1]</xref>
###xml 270 284 270 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 363 377 363 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 448 451 448 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Horwitz1">[2]</xref>
###xml 607 610 607 610 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Isberg1">[3]</xref>
###xml 706 720 706 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 929 943 929 943 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 949 963 949 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1020 1023 1020 1023 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Laguna1">[4]</xref>
###xml 1094 1097 1094 1097 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Laguna1">[4]</xref>
###xml 28 50 <span type="species:ncbi:446">Legionella pneumophila</span>
###xml 125 139 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 270 284 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 355 361 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 363 377 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 706 720 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 929 943 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 949 963 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
The intracellular bacterium Legionella pneumophila has become a valuable model for the study of immunosurveillance pathways. L. pneumophila is a motile gram-negative bacterium that is the cause of a severe pneumonia called Legionnaires' Disease [1]. In the environment, L. pneumophila is believed to replicate in various species of freshwater amoebae. In humans, L. pneumophila causes disease by replicating within alveolar macrophages in the lung [2]. Replication in macrophages and amoebae requires a type IV secretion system that the bacterium uses to inject effector proteins into the host cell cytosol [3]. These effectors are believed to orchestrate the creation of an intracellular vacuole in which L. pneumophila can replicate. Interestingly, there appears to be considerable redundancy among the effectors, and there are few examples of single effector mutations that have a large effect on intracellular replication of L. pneumophila. One L. pneumophila effector required for intracellular replication is SdhA [4], but the mechanism by which SdhA acts on host cells remains uncertain [4].
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 53 67 53 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 98 101 98 101 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Archer1">[5]</xref>
###xml 102 105 102 105 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Hawn1">[6]</xref>
###xml 106 109 106 109 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Hawn2">[7]</xref>
###xml 110 113 110 113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Shin1">[8]</xref>
###xml 253 267 253 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 401 404 401 404 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Amer1">[9]</xref>
###xml 405 409 405 409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Lightfield1">[10]</xref>
###xml 410 414 410 414 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Molofsky1">[11]</xref>
###xml 415 419 415 419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ren1">[12]</xref>
###xml 420 424 420 424 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Zamboni1">[13]</xref>
###xml 426 440 426 440 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 635 639 635 639 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Opitz1">[14]</xref>
###xml 640 644 640 644 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Stetson1">[15]</xref>
###xml 674 688 674 688 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 737 741 737 741 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Coers1">[16]</xref>
###xml 829 833 829 833 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Coers1">[16]</xref>
###xml 834 838 834 838 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Schiavoni1">[17]</xref>
###xml 870 874 870 874 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Opitz1">[14]</xref>
###xml 53 67 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 253 267 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 426 440 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 674 688 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
A variety of immunosurveillance pathways that detect L. pneumophila infection have been described [5],[6],[7],[8]. The best characterized cytosolic immunosurveillance pathway requires the host proteins Naip5 and Ipaf to detect the cytosolic presence of L. pneumophila flagellin, leading to activation of caspase-1, rapid pyroptotic macrophage death, and efficient restriction of bacterial replication [9],[10],[11],[12],[13]. L. pneumophila has also been observed to induce transcriptional activation of type I interferon (IFN) genes in macrophages and epithelial-like cell lines by a mechanism that remains incompletely characterized [14],[15]. Induction of type I IFNs by L. pneumophila is independent of the flagellin-sensing pathway [16], but also appears to contribute to restriction of bacterial replication in macrophages [16],[17] and epithelial-like cell lines [14].
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 103 107 103 107 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Stetson2">[18]</xref>
###xml 385 389 361 365 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Pichlmair1">[19]</xref>
###xml 501 505 477 481 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Yoneyama1">[20]</xref>
###xml 581 585 557 561 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Seth1">[21]</xref>
###xml 586 590 562 566 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Kawai1">[22]</xref>
###xml 591 595 567 571 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Xu1">[23]</xref>
###xml 596 600 572 576 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Meylan1">[24]</xref>
###xml 601 605 577 581 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Sun1">[25]</xref>
###xml 707 711 683 687 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Stetson1">[15]</xref>
###xml 712 716 688 692 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ishii1">[26]</xref>
###xml 731 736 707 712 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 814 819 790 795 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 862 866 838 842 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Sun1">[25]</xref>
###xml 972 976 948 952 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ishii1">[26]</xref>
###xml 977 981 953 957 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Cheng1">[27]</xref>
###xml 1077 1081 1053 1057 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ablasser1">[28]</xref>
###xml 1082 1086 1058 1062 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 1423 1427 1399 1403 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Takaoka1">[30]</xref>
###xml 1428 1432 1404 1408 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Wang1">[31]</xref>
###xml 1438 1442 1414 1418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Zbp1</italic>
###xml 1502 1506 1478 1482 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ishii2">[32]</xref>
###xml 1777 1781 1753 1757 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Karaolis1">[33]</xref>
###xml 1782 1786 1758 1762 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-McWhirter1">[34]</xref>
###xml 1787 1791 1763 1767 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Roberts1">[35]</xref>
###xml 747 751 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1453 1457 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Type I IFNs are an important class of cytokines that orchestrate diverse immune responses to pathogens [18]. Encoded by a single IFNbeta gene as well as multiple IFNalpha and other (e.g., IFNepsilon, kappa, delta, zeta) genes, type I IFNs are transcriptionally induced by a number of immunosurveillance pathways, including Toll-like receptors (TLRs) and a variety of cytosolic sensors [19]. For example, cytosolic RNA is recognized by two distinct helicase and CARD-containing sensors, RIG-I and MDA5 [20], that signal through the adaptor IPS-1 (also called MAVS, CARDIF, or VISA) [21],[22],[23],[24],[25]. The cytosolic presence of DNA also induces type I IFNs, but this phenomenon is less well understood [15],[26]. Studies with Ips-1-deficient mice have indicated that cytosolic DNA can signal independently of Ips-1 in many cell types, including macrophages [25]. However, cytosolic responses to DNA appear to require IPS-1 in certain cell types, including 293T cells [26],[27]. Indeed, two recent reports have described a pathway by which AT-rich DNA can signal via IPS-1 [28],[29]. In this pathway, DNA is transcribed by RNA polymerase III to form an RNA intermediate that can be sensed by RIG-I. The RNA Pol III pathway appears to be operational in macrophages, but is redundant with other DNA-sensing pathways in these cells. A couple of reports have proposed that DAI (also called ZBP-1) is a cytosolic DNA-sensor [30],[31], but Zbp1-deficient mice appear to respond normally to cytosolic DNA [32], consistent with the existence of multiple cytosolic sensors for DNA. Other small molecule compounds, such as cyclic-di-GMP and DMXAA, can also trigger cytosolic immunosurveillance pathways leading to induction of type I IFNs, but these remain to be fully characterized [33],[34],[35].
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 176 180 176 180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Pichlmair1">[19]</xref>
###xml 225 230 225 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 557 570 557 570 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Streptococcus</italic>
###xml 570 574 570 574 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Mancuso1">[36]</xref>
###xml 693 715 693 715 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Listeria monocytogenes</italic>
###xml 753 757 753 757 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Leber1">[37]</xref>
###xml 758 762 758 762 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-ORiordan1">[38]</xref>
###xml 768 773 768 773 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 820 836 820 836 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. monocytogenes</italic>
###xml 870 874 870 874 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Auerbuch1">[39]</xref>
###xml 875 879 875 879 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Carrero1">[40]</xref>
###xml 880 884 880 884 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-OConnell1">[41]</xref>
###xml 922 944 922 944 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Francisella tularensis</italic>
###xml 946 972 946 972 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mycobacterium tuberculosis</italic>
###xml 974 990 974 990 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Brucella abortus</italic>
###xml 1004 1017 1004 1017 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Streptococcus</italic>
###xml 1103 1107 1103 1107 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-CharrelDennis1">[42]</xref>
###xml 1108 1112 1108 1112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Henry1">[43]</xref>
###xml 1113 1117 1113 1117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Roux1">[44]</xref>
###xml 1118 1122 1118 1122 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Stanley1">[45]</xref>
###xml 182 186 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
###xml 693 715 <span type="species:ncbi:1639">Listeria monocytogenes</span>
###xml 784 788 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 820 836 <span type="species:ncbi:1639">L. monocytogenes</span>
###xml 865 869 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 922 944 <span type="species:ncbi:263">Francisella tularensis</span>
###xml 946 972 <span type="species:ncbi:1773">Mycobacterium tuberculosis</span>
###xml 974 990 <span type="species:ncbi:235">Brucella abortus</span>
Type I IFNs are typically considered antiviral cytokines that act locally to induce an antiviral state and systemically to induce cellular innate and adaptive immune responses [19]. Mice deficient in the type I IFN receptor (Ifnar) are unable to respond to type I IFNs, and are highly susceptible to viral infections. Interestingly, most bacterial infections also trigger production of type I IFNs, but the physiological significance of type I IFNs in immune defense against bacteria is complex. Type I IFN appears to protect against infection with group B Streptococcus[36], but this is not the case for many other bacterial infections. For example, the intracellular gram-positive bacterium Listeria monocytogenes induces a potent type I IFN response [37],[38], but Ifnar-deficient mice are actually more resistant to L. monocytogenes infection than are wildtype mice [39],[40],[41]. Many bacterial pathogens, including Francisella tularensis, Mycobacterium tuberculosis, Brucella abortus, and group B Streptococcus, induce type I IFN production by macrophages via a cytosolic TLR-independent pathway [42],[43],[44],[45], but the bacterial ligands and host sensors required for the interferon response of macrophages to these bacteria remain unknown.
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 52 66 52 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 236 240 236 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Stetson1">[15]</xref>
###xml 311 315 311 315 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Stetson1">[15]</xref>
###xml 316 320 316 320 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ishii1">[26]</xref>
###xml 411 415 411 415 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Vogel1">[46]</xref>
###xml 446 460 446 460 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 516 520 516 520 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Stetson1">[15]</xref>
###xml 630 644 630 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 681 685 681 685 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Opitz1">[14]</xref>
###xml 901 915 901 915 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 915 919 915 919 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Opitz1">[14]</xref>
###xml 952 966 952 966 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1006 1013 1006 1013 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 52 66 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 446 460 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 630 644 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 648 653 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 901 915 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 952 966 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
It was demonstrated that induction of type I IFN by L. pneumophila in macrophages did not require bacterial replication or signaling through the TLR-adaptors MyD88 or Trif, but did require the bacterial Dot/Icm type IV secretion system [15]. Because the IFN response could be recapitulated with transfected DNA [15],[26] and because Dot/Icm system has been shown to conjugate DNA plasmids to recipient bacteria [46], it was proposed that perhaps L. pneumophila induced type I IFN via a cytosolic DNA-sensing pathway [15]. Another report used RNA interference to implicate the signaling adaptor IPS-1 (MAVS) in the IFN response to L. pneumophila in human A549 epithelial-like cells [14]. However, the significance of this latter finding is unclear since RNAi-mediated knockdown of RIG-I and MDA5, the two sensor proteins directly upstream of IPS-1, did not have an effect on induction of type I IFN by L. pneumophila[14]. Moreover, the A549 response to L. pneumophila may be distinct from the macrophage or in vivo response.
###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 35 49 35 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 106 110 106 110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 258 263 258 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 334 348 334 348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 348 352 348 352 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 470 484 470 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 570 584 570 584 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 610 614 610 614 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 664 668 664 668 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ablasser1">[28]</xref>
###xml 669 673 669 673 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-McWhirter1">[34]</xref>
###xml 750 755 750 755 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 791 805 791 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 932 937 932 937 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 950 955 950 955 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 980 984 980 984 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 1026 1040 1026 1040 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 35 49 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 274 279 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 334 348 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 470 484 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 570 584 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 769 774 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 791 805 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1026 1040 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Recently, one report proposed that L. pneumophila DNA was recognized in the cytosol by RNA polymerase III [29], resulting in the production of an RNA intermediate that triggered IFN production via the IPS-1 pathway. Apparently consistent with this proposal, Ips-1-deficient mouse macrophages did not produce type I IFN in response to L. pneumophila[29]. Moreover, since Pol III acts preferentially on AT-rich substrates, it is plausible that Pol III would recognize the L. pneumophila genome, which has a high proportion (62%) of A:T basepairs. However, the response to L. pneumophila DNA was not investigated [29]. In addition, the same report, as well as others [28],[34], observed that the type I IFN response to AT-rich (or any other) DNA is not Ips-1-dependent in mouse cells. Thus, if L. pneumophila DNA was reaching the cytosol, the simplest prediction would be that the resulting type I IFN response would be independent of Ips-1, instead of Ips-1-dependent, as was shown [29]. Thus, the mechanism of IFN induction by L. pneumophila remains unclear.
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 119 133 119 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 170 174 170 174 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Opitz1">[14]</xref>
###xml 175 179 175 179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 194 199 194 199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 263 277 263 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 288 296 288 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 347 352 347 352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 403 410 403 410 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 519 531 519 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1, Rig-i</italic>
###xml 536 540 536 540 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 596 610 596 610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 714 728 714 728 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 753 767 753 767 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 794 799 794 799 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 800 804 800 804 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 805 810 805 810 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 877 882 877 882 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 905 919 905 919 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 964 978 964 978 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 996 1001 996 1001 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 1078 1092 1078 1092 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1123 1137 1123 1137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1382 1386 1382 1386 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Pichlmair1">[19]</xref>
###xml 1559 1564 1559 1564 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1591 1605 1591 1605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 119 133 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 263 277 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 596 610 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 714 728 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 753 767 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 905 919 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 964 978 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1078 1092 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1123 1137 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1591 1605 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
In the present study, we sought to define bacterial and host factors controlling the macrophage type I IFN response to L. pneumophila. In agreement with previous studies [14],[29], we find that Ips-1 is required for optimal induction of type I IFN in response to L. pneumophila infection in vitro. We extend this observation by demonstrating that Ips-1 also contributes to the type I IFN response in an in vivo model of Legionnaires' Disease. Furthermore, we provide the first evidence that two RNA sensors upstream of Ips-1, Rig-i and Mda5, are involved in the macrophage interferon response to L. pneumophila. Importantly, however, we did not observe a role for the Pol III pathway in the type I IFN response to L. pneumophila. Instead, we found that L. pneumophila genomic DNA stimulates an Ips-1/Mda5/Rig-i-independent IFN response in macrophages, which contrasts with the Ips-1-dependent response to L. pneumophila infection. On the other hand, we found that L. pneumophila RNA stimulated a Rig-i-dependent IFN response. Thus, our data are consistent with a model in which L. pneumophila RNA, or host RNA, rather than L. pneumophila DNA, is the primary ligand that stimulates the host IFN response. We also investigated whether bacterial factors that modulate the host type I IFN response. Although numerous viral proteins that interfere with IFN signaling have been described [19], similar bacterial proteins have not been documented. It is therefore interesting that we were able to identify a secreted bacterial effector, SdhA, as an inhibitor of the Ips-1-dependent IFN response to L. pneumophila. Taken together, our findings provide surprising evidence that cytosolic RNA-sensing pathways are not specific for viral infections but can also respond to bacterial infections, and moreover, our data provide a specific example of a bacterial factor that suppresses the host IFN response.
###end p 12

###xml 1131 1140 1127 1136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 1170 1184 1166 1180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1204 1207 1200 1203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">via</italic>
###xml 99 113 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 280 294 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 327 341 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 636 650 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1064 1078 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1170 1184 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
We hypothesized that a cytosolic innate immune sensing pathway controls the type I IFN response to L. pneumophila. To test this hypothesis, we determined whether macrophages deficient in known cytosolic RNA and DNA sensing pathway components can induce type I IFNs in response to L. pneumophila. Macrophages were infected with L. pneumophila at a multiplicity of infection (MOI) of 1 and induction of interferon beta (Ifnb) message was analyzed by quantitative RT-PCR after 4 hours (Figure 1A-D). As previously reported [29], Ips-1-/- macrophages showed a significantly reduced induction of Ifnb in response to infection with wild type L. pneumophila compared to Ips-1+/+ macrophages (p<0.05; Figure 1A). Induction of Ifnb was not completely eliminated in Ips-1-/- macrophages, however, as Irf3-/- macrophages exhibited an even lower induction of Ifnb compared to Ips-1-/- (p<0.05; Figure 1A). Consistent with previous reports [15], we found that the Dot/Icm type IV secretion system was required to elicit the macrophage type I interferon response since Deltadot L. pneumophila did not induce a robust type I interferon response (Figure 1A). These results suggest that L. pneumophila induces type I IFN via a cytosolic RNA immunosurveillance pathway that involves the adaptor Ips-1.
###end p 15
###begin title 16
###xml 88 102 88 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 88 102 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
The cytosolic RNA-sensing pathway is involved in the host type I interferon response to L. pneumophila.
###end title 16

###xml 43 57 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 195 209 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 601 615 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 642 656 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 783 797 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1046 1060 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1718 1732 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1823 1837 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2072 2086 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2163 2177 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2225 2239 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2344 2358 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2512 2526 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
(A) Induction of interferon beta (Ifnb) by L. pneumophila is largely dependent on Ips-1. Bone marrow derived Ips-1+/+, Ips-1-/-, and Irf3-/- macrophages were infected with wild type and Deltadot L. pneumophila at a multiplicity of infection (MOI) of 1. Ifnb induction was analyzed by quantitative RT-PCR 4 hours post infection. Ifnb message was normalized to ribosomal protein rps17 levels. Differences in Ifnb transcript induction were statistically significant in Ips-1+/+versus Ips-1-/- macrophages (*, p<0.05) and Ips-1-/- versus Irf3-/- (*, p<0.05, Student's t-test) when infected with wild type L. pneumophila. (B) Induction of Ifnb by L. pneumophila is partially dependent on Mda5. Bone marrow derived Mda5+/+ and Mda5-/- macrophages were infected with wild type and Deltadot L. pneumophila at a multiplicity of infection (MOI) of 1. Ifnb induction was assessed by quantitative RT-PCR as in (A). Differences in Ifnb induction were statistically significant (*, p<0.05, Student's t-test) between Mda5+/+ and Mda5-/- infected with wild type L. pneumophila. (C) Retroviral transduction of a Rig-i shRNA, but not the control shRNA, knocks down expression of Rig-i in MyD88-/-Trif-/- immortalized macrophages. Stable transduction of MyD88-/-Trif-/- immortalized macrophages was performed with a retroviral vector containing a control and Rig-i shRNA. Level of Rig-i knockdown was determined by quantitative RT-PCR under uninfected, infected, and poly I:C stimulation conditions. Differences in Rig-i transcript levels were statistically significant (*, p<0.05, Students t-test) under resting, infected, and ligand-stimulated conditions. (D) Rig-i is involved in the host type I interferon response to infection with L. pneumophila. Rig-i knockdown leads to reduced Ifnb expression in response to infection with DeltaflaA L. pneumophila, as well as stimulation with poly I:C. Quantitative RT-PCR was carried out 4 hours post infection. Control knockdown macrophages induced a statistically significant (*, p<0.05) higher level of Ifnb transcript in response to DeltaflaA L. pneumophila and poly I:C. No significant difference was found in uninfected or Deltadot L. pneumophila infected macrophages. (E) Induction of Ifnb by L. pneumophila is independent of Zbp-1 (Dai). Bone marrow derived Zbp-1+/+ and Zbp-1-/- macrophages were infected with L. pneumophila strains and analyzed for Ifnb induction as in (A) and (B). Differences in Ifnb transcript levels between Zbp-1+/+ and Zbp-1-/- macrophages infected with L. pneumophila were not statistically significant (ns, p>0.1, Student's t-test).
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 71 76 71 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 137 151 137 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 290 294 290 294 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Opitz1">[14]</xref>
###xml 317 321 317 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 321 324 321 324 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 347 356 347 356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 389 393 389 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 429 432 429 432 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 425 432 425 432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 468 471 468 471 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dot</italic>
###xml 538 542 538 542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 542 545 542 545 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 137 151 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
We hypothesized that a cytosolic RNA sensor that functions upstream of Ips-1 could be involved in the type I interferon host response to L. pneumophila. However, knockdown experiments in A549 cells previously failed to reveal a role for the known sensors (MDA5 and RIG-I) upstream of IPS-1 [14]. Therefore, we tested Mda5-/- knockout macrophages (Figure 1B) and found reduced induction of Ifnb message as compared to control Mda5+/+ macrophages. Importantly, however, Dot-dependent induction of type I IFN was not completely abolished in Mda5-/- macrophages, implying that other redundant pathways are also involved.
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 0 5 0 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 64 69 64 69 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 69 72 69 72 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 221 226 221 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 336 345 336 345 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g001">Figure 1C</xref>
###xml 357 362 357 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 439 453 439 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 455 464 455 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g001">Figure 1D</xref>
###xml 489 506 489 506 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g001">Figures 1C and 1D</xref>
###xml 524 528 520 524 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flaA</italic>
###xml 539 553 535 549 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 687 701 683 697 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 701 705 697 701 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Opitz1">[14]</xref>
###xml 706 710 702 706 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Coers1">[16]</xref>
###xml 827 831 823 827 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Fredericksen1">[47]</xref>
###xml 15 19 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 439 453 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 539 553 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 687 701 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Rig-i knockout mice die as embryos, so we were unable to obtain Rig-i-/- knockout macrophages. To circumvent this problem, we stably transduced immortalized macrophages with a retrovirus expressing an shRNA to knock down Rig-i expression. Quantitative RT-PCR demonstrated that the knockdown was effective, even in infected macrophages (Figure 1C), and that Rig-i knockdown had a significant effect on the induction of type I interferon by L. pneumophila (Figure 1D). In the experiments in Figures 1C and 1D we used the DeltaflaA strain of L. pneumophila, but similar results were obtained with wildtype, and it was previously shown that flagellin is not required for the IFN response to L. pneumophila[14],[16]. It is unusual, but not unprecedented, that a pathogen would stimulate both the RIG-I and MDA5 RNA-sensing pathways [47].
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 100 104 100 104 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Takaoka1">[30]</xref>
###xml 105 109 105 109 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Wang1">[31]</xref>
###xml 216 230 216 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 250 254 250 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Zbp1</italic>
###xml 254 257 254 257 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 281 295 281 295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 327 331 327 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 349 352 349 352 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 345 352 345 352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Zbp1<sup>+/+</sup></italic>
###xml 357 361 357 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Zbp1</italic>
###xml 361 364 361 364 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 378 387 378 387 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g001">Figure 1E</xref>
###xml 516 530 516 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 216 230 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 281 295 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 516 530 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
At present, only one candidate cytosolic DNA sensor involved in the IFN response has been described [30],[31]. To determine whether this sensor, called Dai (or Zpb1), is involved in the type I interferon response to L. pneumophila, we tested whether Zbp1-/- macrophages respond to L. pneumophila. We observed similar levels of Ifnb induction in Zbp1+/+ and Zbp1-/- macrophages (Figure 1E). Taken together, these results imply that the RNA sensors Rig-i and Mda5, but not the DNA sensor Zbp1, are involved in sensing L. pneumophila infection.
###end p 20
###begin p 21
###xml 71 76 71 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 80 84 80 84 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 139 144 139 144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 144 147 144 147 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 160 164 160 164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Coers1">[16]</xref>
###xml 183 188 183 188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 188 191 188 191 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 196 200 196 200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 200 203 200 203 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 235 249 235 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 320 325 317 322 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 329 333 326 330 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 361 375 358 372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 384 393 381 390 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000665.s001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 235 249 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 361 375 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
We tested whether loss of signaling through the RNA sensing components Ips-1 or Mda5 could mimic the previously observed permissiveness of Ifnar-/- macrophages [16]. However, neither Ips-1-/- nor Mda5-/- macrophages were permissive to L. pneumophila, suggesting that the low levels of IFNbeta produced in the absence of Ips-1 or Mda5 are sufficient to restrict L. pneumophila growth (Figure S1).
###end p 21
###begin title 22
###xml 73 87 73 87 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 73 87 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
The type IV secreted effector SdhA suppresses induction of interferon by L. pneumophila
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 81 95 81 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 162 176 162 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 200 207 200 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mariner</italic>
###xml 243 247 243 247 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ren1">[12]</xref>
###xml 299 304 299 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MyD88</italic>
###xml 304 307 304 307 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 307 311 307 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Trif</italic>
###xml 311 314 311 314 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 468 472 468 472 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Jiang1">[48]</xref>
###xml 540 558 536 554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dot L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 789 796 785 792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dot/Icm</italic>
###xml 814 842 810 838 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">icmB, icmC, icmD, icmX, icmJ</italic>
###xml 81 95 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 162 176 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 544 558 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
To identify bacterial components that modulate the type I interferon response to L. pneumophila, we conducted a transposon mutagenesis screen. The LP02 strain of L. pneumophila was mutagenized with a mariner transposon as described previously [12]. Individual transposon mutants were used to infect MyD88-/-Trif-/- bone marrow-derived macrophages at an MOI of 1, and after approximately 16 hours, supernatants were collected and overlayed on type I IFN reporter cells [48]. Induction of type I IFN was compared to wild type (LP02) and Deltadot L. pneumophila controls. We tested approximately 2000 independent mutants and isolated eight mutants that were confirmed to be defective in induction of type I IFN. All these mutants harbored insertions in genes required for the function of the Dot/Icm apparatus (e.g., icmB, icmC, icmD, icmX, icmJ), thereby validating the screen.
###end p 23
###begin p 24
###xml 233 237 233 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 265 268 265 268 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Laguna1">[4]</xref>
###xml 345 354 345 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g002">Figure 2A</xref>
###xml 445 448 445 448 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Laguna1">[4]</xref>
Interestingly, a single transposon mutant, 11C11, was found that consistently hyperinduced the type I interferon response. The transposon insertion mapped to the 3' end (nucleotide position 3421 of the open reading frame) of a gene, sdhA, that was previously shown [4] to encode a type IV secreted effector protein of 1429 amino acids (166kDa) (Figure 2A). SdhA has previously been shown to be essential for bacterial replication in macrophages [4], but a connection to type I IFNs was not previously noted.
###end p 24
###begin title 25
###xml 73 87 73 87 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 73 87 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
The type IV secreted effector SdhA suppresses induction of interferon by L. pneumophila.
###end title 25

(A) The 11C11 mutant harbors a transposon insertion in sdhA. The transposon insertion site is in the 3' end of the open reading frame of the sdhA locus at nucleotide position 3421. (B) A clean deletion mutant of sdhA recapitulates the 11C11 transposon mutant and hyperinduces type I interferon. Bone marrow derived Myd88-/-Trif-/- macrophages were infected with stationary phase L. pneumophila strains at a MOI of 1. Cell supernatants were harvested 8 hours post infection and assayed for type I interferon induction by an L929-ISRE luciferase bioassay. Type I interferon levels were determined by generating a standard curve with recombinant IFNbeta An unmarked clean deletion of sdhA was compared to wild type, Deltadot, the transposon mutant 11C11, and a triple deletion of sdhA and the two L. pneumophila paralogs, sidH and sdhB. Differences in IFNbeta induction were statistically significant between WT L. pneumophila and the transposon mutant 11C11 (***, p<0.0005, Student's t-test). Differences between 11C11, DeltasdhA and DeltasdhADeltasdhBDeltasidH were not statistically significant (ns, p>0.05, Student's t-test). (C) A clean deletion mutant of sdhA recapitulates the 11C11 transposon mutant and hyperinduces transcriptional activation of Ifnb. Bone marrow derived Myd88-/-Trif-/- macrophages were infected with wild type, Deltadot, DeltasdhA, 11C11, DeltasdhADeltasdhBDeltasidH stationary phase L. pneumophila and transcriptional induction of Ifnb was analyzed by quantitative RT-PCR. (D) Complementation of the sdhA mutant results in loss of the Ifnb hyperinduction phenotype. MyD88-/-Trif-/- BMDM were infected at an MOI of 1 with DeltaflaA, Deltadot, DeltaflaADeltasdhA and DeltaflaADeltasdhA L. pneumophila carrying vector or a plasmid expressing full length SdhA. Expression of Ifnb message was assessed by quantitative RT-PCR 4 hours post infection.

###begin p 27
###xml 79 83 79 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 159 163 159 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 165 174 165 174 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g002">Figure 2B</xref>
###xml 208 227 204 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 294 308 290 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 339 343 335 339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 352 356 348 352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sidH</italic>
###xml 361 365 357 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhB</italic>
###xml 398 402 390 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 407 411 395 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhB</italic>
###xml 416 421 400 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sidH,</italic>
###xml 457 461 441 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 577 581 554 558 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 586 590 559 563 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhB</italic>
###xml 595 599 564 568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sidH</italic>
###xml 609 613 574 578 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 615 624 580 589 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g002">Figure 2B</xref>
###xml 675 679 640 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 717 726 682 691 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g002">Figure 2C</xref>
###xml 740 744 705 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 831 835 792 796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 853 857 814 818 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 877 880 838 841 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Laguna1">[4]</xref>
###xml 979 983 936 940 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 1019 1028 976 985 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g002">Figure 2D</xref>
###xml 1141 1155 1098 1112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 213 227 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 294 308 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1141 1155 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
To confirm that the hyperinduction of type I interferon was due to mutation of sdhA, the 11C11 transposon mutant was compared to an unmarked clean deletion of sdhA (Figure 2B). Both the 11C11 mutant and DeltasdhA L. pneumophila showed similar levels of hyperinduction of type I interferon. The L. pneumophila genome contains 2 paralogs of sdhA, called sidH and sdhB. A triple knockout strain, DeltasdhADeltasdhBDeltasidH, was compared to single deletion of sdhA to determine if either paralog regulated the induction of type I IFNs. Similar levels of IFNbeta were induced DeltasdhADeltasdhBDeltasidH and DeltasdhA (Figure 2B). Similar results were obtained when induction of Ifnb was assessed by quantitative RT-PCR (Figure 2C). A role for sdhA in regulating the interferon response was further confirmed by complementing the DeltasdhA mutation with an sdhA expression plasmid [4]. As expected, the complemented strain induced significantly less type I IFN than the control DeltasdhA strain harboring an empty plasmid (Figure 2D). These results indicate that SdhA functions, directly or indirectly, to repress the induction of type I IFN by L. pneumophila.
###end p 27
###begin title 28
###xml 36 40 36 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
Hyperinduction of type I IFN by the sdhA mutant involves the cytosolic RNA-sensing pathway
###end title 28

###xml 551 556 539 544 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 556 559 544 547 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 582 591 570 579 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g003">Figure 3A</xref>

###xml 804 813 792 801 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g003">Figure 3B</xref>
###xml 829 833 817 821 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 833 836 821 824 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 886 891 874 879 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb,</italic>
###xml 928 932 916 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 974 978 958 962 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 989 994 973 978 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 1060 1069 1044 1053 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g003">Figure 3C</xref>
###xml 1099 1103 1083 1087 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 1116 1125 1100 1109 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g003">Figure 3D</xref>
###xml 1147 1151 1131 1135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 1165 1169 1149 1153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 1169 1172 1153 1156 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1187 1193 1171 1177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i,</italic>
###xml 1278 1282 1262 1266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 1299 1303 1283 1287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 1335 1344 1319 1328 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g003">Figure 3B</xref>
###xml 158 172 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 314 328 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 390 404 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
It was possible that DeltasdhA mutants hyperinduced type I IFN via a pathway distinct from the normal cytosolic RNA-sensing pathway that responds to wildtype L. pneumophila. Therefore, to determine whether hyperinduction of type I interferon by DeltasdhA occurs through the same pathway that responds to wild type L. pneumophila, we infected Ips-1-/- and Mda5-/- macrophages with DeltasdhA L. pneumophila. Induction of Ifnb message was determined by quantitative RT-PCR. The hyperinduction of Ifnb seen in Ips-1+/+ macrophages was almost abolished in Ips-1-/- macrophages (p<0.001; Figure 3A). As a control, induction of Ifnb by poly I:C, a double-stranded synthetic RNA analog, was also Ips-1-dependent as expected. Similarly, the hyperinduction of Ifnb was also reduced in Mda5-/- macrophages (p<0.01; Figure 3B). However, the Mda5-/- macrophages still induced significant amounts of Ifnb, suggesting that the requirement for Mda5 is not complete. We also tested the DeltasdhA mutant in Rig-i knockdown macrophages. Rig-i knockdown appeared to be effective (Figure 3C) and specifically diminished Ifnb expression (Figure 3D). Thus, the residual Ifnb induction in Mda5-/- may be due to Rig-i, or to another uncharacterized pathway. As a control, Theiler's virus (TMEV) induced Ifnb in a completely Mda5-dependent manner, as expected (Figure 3B).
###end p 29
###begin title 30
###xml 32 36 32 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 95 100 95 100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 102 107 102 107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 113 117 113 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
Hyperinduction of type I IFN by sdhA mutants involves cytosolic RNA sensing pathway components Ips-1, Rig-i, and Mda5.
###end title 30

###xml 1526 1533 1474 1481 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5<sup>+/+</sup></italic>

###xml 2247 2266 2187 2206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 2447 2451 2387 2391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 2490 2509 2426 2445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 2586 2604 2518 2536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dot L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 40 54 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
