###xml 446 460 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 639 653 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 777 791 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 939 953 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1274 1288 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1408 1422 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2140 2154 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2252 2266 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2279 2291 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">Sendai virus</span>
###xml 2495 2509 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2514 2526 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">Sendai virus</span>
###xml 2590 2604 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
(A) Hyperinduction of Ifnb by DeltasdhA L. pneumophila is largely dependent on Ips-1. Bone marrow derived Ips-1+/+ and Ips-1-/- macrophages were infected with wild type, Deltadot, and DeltasdhA L. pneumophila at an MOI of 1. Ips-1+/+ and Ips-1-/- macrophages were transfected with 1.0 microg/ml poly I:C. 4 hours post infection and stimulation, macrophages were harvested and assessed for Ifnb induction as in Figure 1. Ips-1+/+ infected with WT L. pneumophila induced statistically significant higher levels of Ifnb transcript than Ips-1-/- (**, p<0.005, Student's t-test). The same phenotype was seen in Ips-1+/+ infected with DeltasdhA L. pneumophila (**, p<0.005) and transfected with poly I:C (*, p<0.05) when compared to Ips-1-/-. (B) Hyperinduction of Ifnb by DeltasdhA L. pneumophila is partially dependent on Mda5. Bone marrow derived Mda5+/+ and Mda5-/- macrophages were infected with DeltaflaA, Deltadot, and DeltaflaADeltasdhA L. pneumophila at an MOI of 1. Theiler's virus (TMEV) was overlaid onto Mda5+/+ and Mda5-/- macrophages. 4 hours post bacterial and viral infection, macrophages were harvested and assessed for Ifnb induction by qRT-PCR as in Figure 1. Ifnb message was induced statistically significantly in Mda5+/+ macrophages infected with DeltaflaA L. pneumophila versus Mda5-/- (*, p<0.05, Student's t-test). Mda5+/+ also responded statistically significantly to DeltaflaADeltasdhA L. pneumophila over Mda5-/- (*, p<0.05, Student's t-test), while Theiler's virus elicited a robust Ifnb response from Mda5+/+ not seen in Mda5-/- (***, p<0.005, Student's t-test). (C) Retroviral transduction of a Rig-i shRNA, but not the control shRNA, knocks down expression of Rig-i. MyD88-/-Trif-/- immortalized macrophages were stably transduced with retroviral vector containing a control and Rig-i shRNA. Level of Rig-i knockdown was determined by quantitative RT-PCR under uninfected and infected conditions. Differences in Rig-i transcript levels were statistically significant (*, p<0.05, Students t-test) under resting and infected conditions. (D) Rig-i is involved in the hyperinduction of type I interferon by DeltasdhA L. pneumophila. Rig-i knockdown leads to reduced Ifnb expression in response to infection with WT and DeltasdhA L. pneumophila, as well as Sendai virus. Quantitative RT-PCR was carried out 4 hours post infection. Control knockdown macrophages induced a statistically significant (*, p<0.05) higher level of Ifnb transcript in response to WT and DeltasdhA L. pneumophila and Sendai virus. No significant difference was found in uninfected or Deltadot L. pneumophila infected macrophages.
###end p 31
###begin title 32
###xml 24 28 20 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
The effects of the DeltasdhA mutant are independent of caspase-1 activation
###end title 32
###begin p 33
###xml 34 38 30 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 158 161 154 157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Laguna1">[4]</xref>
###xml 243 247 235 239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 345 349 337 341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 404 409 396 401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Casp1</italic>
###xml 409 412 401 404 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 599 618 587 606 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 643 648 631 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Casp1</italic>
###xml 648 651 636 639 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 686 690 670 674 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 711 715 695 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 765 774 749 758 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
###xml 807 811 791 795 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 830 835 814 819 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Casp1</italic>
###xml 835 838 819 822 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1003 1008 987 992 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Casp1</italic>
###xml 1106 1110 1086 1090 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 1209 1214 1189 1194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Casp1</italic>
###xml 1214 1217 1194 1197 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1287 1296 1267 1276 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 604 618 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
It was previously shown that DeltasdhA mutants induce a rapid death of infected macrophages that is dependent upon activation of multiple cell death pathways [4]. Consequently, we hypothesized that the hyperinduction of type I IFN by the DeltasdhA mutant might be due to the release of molecules from dying cells, such as DNA, that could induce Ifnb expression. To rule out this explanation, we infected Casp1-/- macrophages, which are resistant to cell death at the early timepoints examined (e.g., 4h post infection), and asked whether type I interferon was still hyperinduced in response to DeltasdhA L. pneumophila. In fact, we found that Casp1-/-macrophages infected with the DeltasdhA mutant hyperinduced Ifnb to levels above that observed in B6 macrophages (Figure 4A). We suspect that the increased Ifnb induction seen in Casp1-/- cells was an indirect consequence of the lower levels of cell death in these cells, and was not due to a specific suppression of type I interferon transcription by Casp1 activation. In any case, our results indicated that the hyperinduction of type I IFN by the DeltasdhA mutant was not due to increased cell death induced by the mutant. As a control, we confirmed that Casp1-/- macrophages were resistant to cell death at the 4h timepoint tested (Figure 4B).
###end p 33
###begin title 34
###xml 19 23 19 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
The effects of the sdhA mutation on type I interferon induction are independent of caspase-1 activation and the type I interferon receptor.
###end title 34
###begin p 35
###xml 125 129 125 129 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 137 141 137 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 179 184 179 184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 184 187 184 187 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 192 197 192 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Casp1</italic>
###xml 197 200 197 200 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 248 251 244 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dot</italic>
###xml 262 281 254 273 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 298 302 290 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 516 521 508 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 521 524 513 516 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 529 534 521 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Casp1</italic>
###xml 534 537 526 529 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 585 588 573 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dot</italic>
###xml 599 618 583 602 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 917 922 901 906 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 922 925 906 909 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 957 976 937 956 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 267 281 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 604 618 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 962 976 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
(A) Type I interferon receptor signaling and caspase1-dependent pyroptotic cell death are not required for superinduction of Ifnb by the sdhA mutant. Bone marrow derived C57BL/6, Ifnar-/- and Casp1-/- macrophages were infected with wild type, Deltadot, and DeltasdhA L. pneumophila at an MOI of 1. Ifnb message was analyzed by qPCR from macrophage RNA harvested 4 hours post infection. (B) Caspase1-dependent pyroptotic cell death occurs independently of the type I interferon receptor. Bone marrow derived C57BL/6, Ifnar-/- and Casp1-/- macrophages were infected with wild type, Deltadot, and DeltasdhA L. pneumophila at an MOI of 1 and release of lactate dehydrogenase (LDH) in cell supernatants was measured 4 hours post infection. Specific cell lysis was calculated as a percentage of detergent lysed cells with spontaneous LDH release subtracted. No statistically significant difference was found between B6 and Ifnar-/- macrophages infected with DeltasdhA L. pneumophila (p>0.1, Student's t-test). ND, not detected.
###end p 35
###begin title 36
SdhA acts independently of the type I IFN receptor
###end title 36
###begin p 37
###xml 13 17 13 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 158 163 155 160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 289 293 286 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 306 310 299 303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 435 439 428 432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 452 456 441 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 467 472 456 461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 472 475 461 464 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 521 525 510 514 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 534 553 519 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 637 642 622 627 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 642 645 627 630 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 670 674 655 659 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 710 729 691 710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 731 740 712 721 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
###xml 539 553 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 715 729 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Induction of Ifnb is often regulated by a positive feedback loop in which initial production of IFNbeta results in signaling through the type I IFN receptor (Ifnar) and synergistically stimulates the production of additional type I IFN. We therefore examined whether the hyperinduction of Ifnb by the DeltasdhA mutant might be due to positive feedback through the type I IFN receptor. To test this possibility we examined induction of Ifnb by the DeltasdhA mutant in Ifnar-/- macrophages. We found that hyperinduction of Ifnb by DeltasdhA L. pneumophila occurs even in the absence of signaling from the type I interferon receptor, since Ifnar-/- macrophages hyperinduce Ifnb in response to infection with DeltasdhA L. pneumophila (Figure 4A).
###end p 37
###begin p 38
###xml 32 36 28 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 79 82 75 78 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Laguna1">[4]</xref>
###xml 134 156 130 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Francisella tularensis</italic>
###xml 254 258 250 254 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Henry1">[43]</xref>
###xml 405 424 397 416 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 426 431 418 423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 431 434 423 426 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 580 585 572 577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 585 588 577 580 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 683 702 671 690 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 766 775 754 763 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 938 957 922 941 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 134 156 <span type="species:ncbi:263">Francisella tularensis</span>
###xml 410 424 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 688 702 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 943 957 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
The mechanism by which the DeltasdhA mutant induces cell death remains unclear [4]. Studies with the intracellular bacterial pathogen Francisella tularensis have demonstrated the existence of a type I IFN-inducible caspase-1-dependent cell death pathway [43]. Therefore, we sought to establish if caspase-1-dependent cell death occurred in the absence of Ifnar signaling in response to wild type and DeltasdhA L. pneumophila. Ifnar-/- macrophages were infected at an MOI of 1 and assayed for release of the intracellular enzyme lactate dehydrogenase (LDH) 4 hours post infection. Ifnar-/- macrophages exhibited similar LDH release as B6 macrophages, whether infected with WT or DeltasdhA L. pneumophila, and this LDH release was dependent upon caspase-1 activation (Figure 4B). These data demonstrate that caspase1-dependent pyroptotic death occurs independently of the type I interferon receptor during infection with wild type and DeltasdhA L. pneumophila.
###end p 38
###begin p 39
###xml 25 29 21 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>

###xml 200 204 192 196 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 250 255 242 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lfnar</italic>
###xml 255 258 247 250 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 299 313 291 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 419 423 411 415 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Coers1">[16]</xref>
###xml 425 430 417 422 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lfnar</italic>
###xml 430 433 422 425 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 482 501 470 489 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flaA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 538 548 526 536 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000665.s002">Figure S2A</xref>
###xml 572 576 556 560 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>

###xml 594 613 570 589 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 661 666 637 642 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 666 669 642 645 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 683 693 659 669 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000665.s002">Figure S2B</xref>
###xml 858 876 830 848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dot L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 904 909 876 881 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>
###xml 909 912 881 884 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 926 936 898 908 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000665.s002">Figure S2E</xref>
###xml 299 313 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 487 501 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 599 613 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 862 876 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Since growth of the DeltasdhA mutant is severely attenuated in macrophages [4], we hypothesized that hyperinduction of type I interferon might contribute to the restriction of replication of the DeltasdhA mutant. To test this hypothesis, we infected lfnar-/- macrophages with luminescent strains of L. pneumophila at an MOI of 0.01 and monitored bacterial replication over a 72 hour time period. As previously reported [16], lfnar-/- macrophages were more permissive to WT and DeltaflaA L. pneumophila as compared to C57BL/6 macrophages (Figure S2A, C). However, the DeltasdhA or DeltaflaADeltasdhA L. pneumophila strains were still significantly restricted in Ifnar-/- macrophages (Figure S2B, D). Thus, SdhA is required for bacterial replication in macrophages primarily via a mechanism independent of its role in suppressing type I IFN. As expected, Deltadot L. pneumophila did not replicate in WT or Ifnar-/- macrophages (Figure S2E).
###end p 39
###begin p 40
###xml 136 140 136 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 443 452 437 446 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000665.s003">Figure S3</xref>
###xml 563 573 554 564 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000665.s003">Figure S3A</xref>
###xml 701 711 689 699 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000665.s003">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 811 821 796 806 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000665.s003">Figure S3C</xref>
###xml 1212 1215 1191 1194 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Laguna1">[4]</xref>
###xml 1265 1275 1244 1254 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
Since SdhA is a secreted effector, we hypothesized that SdhA may act in the host cell cytosol, rather than in the bacterium, to repress Ifnb induction. To test this hypothesis, we co-expressed SdhA with MDA5 or RIG-I, by transient transfection of HEK293T cells, and assessed interferon expression with an IFNbeta-luciferase reporter. Expression of either MDA5 or RIG-I robustly induced the IFNbeta-luc reporter upon stimulation with poly I:C (Figure S3). When SdhA was co-expressed with MDA5, a dose-dependent repression of the IFNbeta-luc reporter was observed (Figure S3A). Co-expression of SdhA also resulted in a dose-dependent repression of RIG-I-dependent induction of the IFNbeta-luc reporter (Figure S3B). However, SdhA co-expression did not affect TRIF-dependent induction of the IFNbeta-luc reporter (Figure S3C), arguing against the possibility that SdhA expression has non-specific effects on IFNbeta-luc induction. These results must be interpreted with caution since the 293T IFNbeta-luc reporter system is highly artificial; moreover, we have not demonstrated a direct interaction of SdhA with signaling components in the RNA-sensing pathway. In fact, the reported effects of SdhA on mitochondria [4] suggest the effect may be somewhat indirect (see Discussion). Nevertheless, the 293T transfection results suggest that SdhA can act in the host cytosol to specifically repress induction of the RIG-I/MDA5 pathway.
###end p 40
###begin title 41
###xml 0 14 0 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 59 64 59 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 0 14 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
L. pneumophila genomic DNA does not appear to stimulate an Ips-1-dependent IFN response
###end title 41
###begin p 42
###xml 72 86 72 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>

###xml 944 958 941 955 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>

###xml 1083 1097 1077 1091 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1180 1194 1174 1188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1250 1264 1244 1258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1316 1325 1310 1319 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
###xml 1359 1373 1353 1367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1492 1506 1486 1500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 72 86 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 199 213 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 381 395 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 511 525 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 866 880 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 944 958 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1083 1097 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1180 1194 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1250 1264 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1359 1373 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1492 1506 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Based on our observation that the host type I IFN response requires the L. pneumophila Dot/Icm type IV secretion system and was at least partly Ips-1, Rig-i, and Mda5-dependent, we hypothesized that L. pneumophila nucleic acids (RNA, DNA or both) might gain access to the macrophage cytosol via the type IV secretion system and induce a host type I interferon response. To test if L. pneumophila nucleic acids are sufficient to induce type I interferon, we transfected MyD88-/-Trif-/- macrophages with purified L. pneumophila genomic DNA or total RNA and determined the induction of type I interferons by bioassay. Poly(dA-dT):poly(dA-dT) (abbreviated as pA:T) was used as a non-CpG containing DNA control and poly I:C was used as an RNA control. Nucleic acid preparations were treated with DNase and/or RNase to eliminate contaminating nucleic acids. Both purified L. pneumophila DNA and the crude RNA preparation induced IFNbeta (Figure 5A). L. pneumophila RNA treated with RNase also induced IFNbeta, presumably due to (contaminating) DNA in the preparation (Figure 5A). However, L. pneumophila RNA treated with DNase induced type I interferon to a level above that induced by L. pneumophila RNA treated with both RNase and DNase, suggesting that L. pneumophila RNA alone can induce type I interferon production (Figure 5A). The induction of type I IFN by L. pneumophila RNA was modest, possibly because bacterial RNA is less stable than DNA. Nevertheless, these results suggest that both L. pneumophila RNA and DNA can induce a type I interferon host response.
###end p 42
###begin title 43
###xml 0 14 0 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 0 14 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
L. pneumophila DNA and RNA stimulate type I IFN production in macrophages.

###xml 2856 2861 2823 2828 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 2861 2864 2828 2831 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2902 2916 2869 2883 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>

###xml 38 52 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>

###xml 1177 1189 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">Sendai virus</span>
###xml 1191 1194 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">SeV</span>
###xml 1447 1461 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1599 1613 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1619 1631 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">Sendai virus</span>
###xml 1633 1636 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">SeV</span>
###xml 2185 2197 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">Sendai virus</span>
###xml 2199 2202 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">SeV</span>
###xml 2478 2492 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2698 2712 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2765 2779 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2902 2916 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 2952 2964 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">Sendai virus</span>
###xml 2966 2969 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">SeV</span>
(A) Purified genomic DNA and RNA from L. pneumophila induces type I interferon independently of MyD88 and Trif. Bone marrow derived Myd88-/-Trif-/- macrophages were stimulated by transfection of 3.3 microg/ml purified L. pneumophila DNA, L. pneumophila RNA, pA:T (DNA), and pI:C (RNA). Nucleic acids were treated with DNase and/or RNase A before transfection. Macrophage supernatants were harvested 8 hours post stimulation and analyzed for IFNbeta levels by L929-ISRE luciferase bioassay. IFNbeta production by DNase-treated L. pneumophila RNA was statistically significantly higher compared to DNase-treated L. pneumophila DNA (**, p<0.005). In addition, RNase A-treated L. pneumophila RNA produced statistically significant lower levels of IFNbeta (***, p<0.0001, Student's t-test) than L. pneumophila RNA and RNase-treated L. pneumophila DNA. (B) Genomic L. pneumophila DNA does not induce type I interferon in a Ips-1-dependent manner. Ips-1-/- and heterozygous littermate bone marrow derived macrophages were stimulated by transfection of 1.0 microg/ml pA:T and purified genomic L. pneumophila DNA. Macrophages were infected with DeltaflaA L. pneumophila at an MOI of 1. Sendai virus (SeV) was overlaid onto Ips-1-/- and heterozygous littermate macrophages. Transcriptional activation of Ifnb was determined by quantitative RT-PCR as described in Figure 1. (C) The viral RNA sensor Mda5 is not required for induction of type I interferon by L. pneumophila DNA. WT (C57BL/6) and Mda5-/- bone marrow derived macrophages were stimulated by transfection of 1.0 microg/ml pA:T and purified genomic L. pneumophila DNA. Sendai virus (SeV) and Theiler's virus (TMEV) were overlaid onto WT and Mda5-/- macrophages. Quantitative RT-PCR was used to determine Ifnb gene expression. (D) Non-CpG containing DNA (pA:T) does not induce Ips-1-dependent Ifnb at all concentrations tested. Ips-1-/- and heterozygous littermate bone marrow derived macrophages were stimulated with a titration of pA:T by transfection of 10, 1.0, 0.1, 0.01 microg/ml pA:T. The difference between Ips-1+/- and Ips-1-/- macrophages transfected with pA:T was not statistically significant (ns, p>0.1, Student's t-test). Sendai virus (SeV) was overlaid onto Ips-1-/- and heterozygous littermate macrophages (**, p<0.005). Cell supernatants were collected 8 hours post stimulation/infection. Induction of type I interferon was determined by L929-ISRE luc bioassay. Units are relative light units (RLU). (E) Genomic L. pneumophila DNA induces type I interferon independently of Ips-1 at all concentrations tested. Ips-1-/- and heterozygous littermate bone marrow derived macrophages were stimulated with a titration of purified genomic L. pneumophila DNA by transfection of 10, 1.0, 0.1, 0.01 microg/ml L. pneumophila DNA. No statistically significant difference was found between Ips-1+/- and Ips-1-/- macrophages transfected with genomic L. pneumophila DNA (ns, p>0.1, Student's t-test). Sendai virus (SeV) was overlaid onto Ips-1-/- and heterozygous littermate controls (**, p<0.005). Macrophage supernatants were collected 8 hours post stimulation/infection. Type I interferon levels were determined by L929-ISRE luc bioassay, units are relative light units (RLU).
###end p 44

###xml 23 37 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 162 167 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 300 314 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 387 401 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 543 557 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 588 600 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">Sendai virus</span>
###xml 700 714 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 779 791 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">Sendai virus</span>
###xml 968 982 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1387 1401 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1516 1530 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1571 1585 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1683 1697 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Next, we determined if L. pneumophila nucleic acids could induce type I interferon in an Ips-1-dependent manner in macrophages. In certain cell types, though not mouse macrophages [34], AT-rich DNA has been shown to induce type I IFN via IPS-1 [26],[27],[28],[29]. It was important to assess whether L. pneumophila DNA, in particular, might signal in an Ips-1-dependent manner since the L. pneumophila type IV secretion system has previously been shown to translocate DNA [46]. Ips-1+/- and Ips-1-/- macrophages were transfected with pA:T and L. pneumophila DNA, as well as infected with Sendai virus, a virus previously determined to induce an Ips-1-dependent IFN response. Stimulation with pA:T or L. pneumophila DNA failed to induce Ifnb in an Ips-1-dependent manner, whereas Sendai virus induced significantly more Ifnb in Ips-1+/- versus Ips-1-/- macrophages (Figure 5B). Similar results were obtained in Mda5-/- macrophages: induction of type I IFN with pA:T or L. pneumophila genomic DNA showed no requirement for Mda5, whereas a control simulation, Theiler's Virus, showed Mda5-dependent induction of IFNbeta, as expected (Figure 5C). It was possible that at high concentrations of DNA, an Ips-1-independent DNA-sensing pathway overwhelmed any putative Ips-1-dependent recognition of DNA. However, induction of Ifnb was independent of Ips-1 even when titrated amounts of pA:T or L. pneumophila genomic DNA were transfected into macrophages (Figure 5D, 5E). Thus, these results suggest that while transfected L. pneumophila DNA robustly induces type I interferon, L. pneumophila genomic DNA does not appear to induce the Ips-1-dependent IFN response that is characteristic of L. pneumophila infection.
###end p 45
###begin title 46
###xml 0 14 0 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 48 57 48 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">via Rig-i</italic>
###xml 0 14 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
L. pneumophila RNA stimulates type I interferon via Rig-i
###end title 46
###begin p 47
###xml 21 35 21 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 85 99 85 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 130 135 130 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 194 199 194 199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 377 382 377 382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 435 440 435 440 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 506 511 506 511 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 555 564 555 564 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 573 587 573 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 647 651 647 651 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 687 692 687 692 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 746 755 746 755 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 797 810 797 810 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophil</italic>
###xml 853 857 853 857 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 861 866 861 866 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 943 952 943 952 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 981 995 981 995 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1011 1017 1011 1017 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i-</italic>
###xml 1105 1110 1105 1110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1110 1113 1110 1113 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1167 1168 1167 1168 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 21 35 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 85 99 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 573 587 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 797 811 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 981 995 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
To determine whether L. pneumophila RNA could be recognized by Rig-i, we transfected L. pneumophila RNA into macrophages in which Rig-i expression had been stably knocked down. Importantly, the Rig-i knockdown was performed in immortalized bone-marrow-derived macrophages that lack MyD88 and Trif, in order to avoid potential activation of known RNA-sensing TLRs. Knockdown of Rig-i was effective under our transfection conditions, as Rig-i message was significantly lower in macrophages transduced with a Rig-i shRNA compared to a control shRNA (p<0.05; Figure 6A). Crude L. pneumophila RNA (which also contains genomic DNA contaminants) induced Ifnb robustly in both control shRNA and Rig-i shRNA macrophages, even upon treatment with RNase A (Figure 6B). However, transfection of DNase-treated L. pneumophila nucleic acids induced significantly less Ifnb in Rig-i knockdown macrophages as compared to control knockdown macrophages (p<0.05; Figure 6B.) This result suggests that L. pneumophila RNA can induce Rig-i-dependent type I interferon. It was not possible to perform a similar experiment in the Ips-1-/- macrophages because these macrophages were MyD88/Trif+ and exhibited background interferon, presumably due to TLR3 signaling.
###end p 47

###xml 45 54 45 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">via Rig-i</italic>
###xml 0 14 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
L. pneumophila RNA induces type I interferon via Rig-i.

###xml 388 393 388 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 421 425 421 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>

###xml 674 693 670 689 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flaA L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 812 826 808 822 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 368 382 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 474 488 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 679 693 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 698 710 <span type="species:ncbi:11191">Sendai virus</span>
###xml 812 826 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
(A) The efficiency of Rig-i knockdown was determined by quantitative RT-PCR under uninfected, viral and bacterial infected, and transfected conditions. Differences in Rig-i transcript levels were statistically significant (*, p<0.05, Students t-test) under resting, infected, and transfected conditions. (B) Rig-i is involved in the host type I interferon response to L. pneumophila RNA. Rig-i knockdown leads to reduced Ifnb expression upon transfection with DNase-treated L. pneumophila RNA. Quantitative RT-PCR was carried out 4 hours post stimulation. Control knockdown macrophages induced a statistically significant (*, p<0.05) higher level of Ifnb transcript in DeltaflaA L. pneumophila and Sendai virus infected macrophages. ###begin p 51
###xml 72 76 72 76 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Wu1">[49]</xref>
###xml 113 127 113 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 127 131 127 131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 154 168 154 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 281 285 281 285 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 367 381 367 381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 418 427 418 427 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 591 596 591 596 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 608 617 608 617 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g007">Figure 7A</xref>
###xml 886 890 886 890 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ablasser1">[28]</xref>
###xml 891 895 891 895 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 1002 1016 1002 1016 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1030 1039 1030 1039 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g007">Figure 7B</xref>
###xml 1064 1078 1064 1078 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1207 1221 1207 1221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1262 1273 1262 1273 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g007">Figure 7C&#8211;E</xref>
###xml 1334 1339 1334 1339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1339 1342 1339 1342 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1385 1399 1385 1399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1413 1422 1413 1422 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000665.s001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 113 127 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 154 168 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 367 381 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1002 1016 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1064 1078 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1207 1221 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1385 1399 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
A recent report found that an inhibitor of RNA polymerase III, ML-60218 [49], blocked the type I IFN response to L. pneumophila[29]. It was proposed that L. pneumophila DNA is translocated into macrophages and transcribed by Pol III into a ligand that could be recognized by RIG-I [29]. In contrast, we did not see an effect of ML-60218 on induction of type I IFN by L. pneumophila in bone marrow-derived macrophages (Figure 7A). The lack of an effect does not appear to be due to redundant recognition by another DNA sensor in macrophages because the interferon induction was still largely Ips-1-dependent (Figure 7A). Because our results with the Pol III inhibitor were negative, we cannot rule out the possibility that the Pol III inhibitor fails to function in macrophages. However, we also tested 293T cells, which express only the Pol III pathway for cytosolic recognition of DNA [28],[29]. As expected, 293T cells responded to pA:T in an ML-60218-inhibitable manner, but did not respond well to L. pneumophila genomic DNA (Figure 7B), again suggesting that L. pneumophila genomic DNA is not an efficient substrate for the Pol III pathway. The Pol III inhibitor also appeared to have little effect on L. pneumophila replication in bone-marrow macrophages (Figure 7C-E). This latter result was expected, since we found that even Ips-1-/- macrophages exhibit normal restriction of L. pneumophila replication (Figure S1), despite significantly reduced IFN induction.
###end p 51

###xml 49 63 49 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 78 92 78 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 49 63 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 78 92 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
The Pol III pathway does not appear to recognize L. pneumophila DNA or affect L. pneumophila replication.
###end title 52

###xml 1151 1156 1142 1147 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1164 1171 1155 1162 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1202 1216 1193 1207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1224 1229 1215 1220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1285 1292 1276 1283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1321 1326 1312 1317 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1415 1419 1406 1410 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Mancuso2">[50]</xref>
###xml 1438 1445 1429 1436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 88 92 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 98 112 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 141 146 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 290 294 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 394 398 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 556 560 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1202 1216 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1240 1244 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
In order to validate our findings in vivo, we infected Ips-1-/- and littermate Ips-1+/- mice with L. pneumophila (2.5x106 LP01 DeltaflaA per mouse, infected intranasally) and assayed type I interferon production in bronchoalveolar lavage fluid 20 hours post infection by bioassay. Ips-1+/- mice induced an IFN response that was statistically significantly greater than the response of Ips-1-/- mice (Student's t-test, p = 0.01; Figure 8A). The difference in IFN production was not explained by a difference in bacterial burden in the Ips-1+/- and Ips-1-/- mice, since both genotypes exhibited similar levels of bacterial colonization (p = 0.76, Student's t-test; Figure 8B). The lack of an effect of Ips-1-deficiency on bacterial replication in vivo was not surprising given that we also failed to observe an effect of Ifnar-deficiency on bacterial replication in vivo (data not shown). We suspect that type II IFN (IFNlambda), which is not made by macrophages in vitro, or another in vivo pathway, may compensate for loss of type I IFN in vivo. Nevertheless, our results provided an important validation of our in vitro studies and affirm a role for Ips-1 in the in vivo type I interferon response to L. pneumophila. Since Ips-1-deficient mice still mounted a measurable IFN response in vivo, it appears that additional Ips-1-independent pathways (e.g., TLR-dependent pathways, possibly involving other cell types [50]) also play a role in vivo.
###end p 55
###begin title 56
###xml 8 13 8 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 21 28 21 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 41 55 41 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 41 55 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Role of Ips-1 in the in vivo response to L. pneumophila.
###end title 56
