###xml 580 594 570 584 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 651 656 641 646 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 656 659 646 649 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 664 669 654 659 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 669 672 659 662 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 717 722 707 712 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 722 725 712 715 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 730 735 720 725 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 735 738 725 728 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 909 923 899 913 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 968 973 958 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 973 976 963 966 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 981 986 971 976 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 986 989 976 979 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 38 52 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 114 118 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 570 574 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 580 594 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 739 743 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 849 854 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 909 923 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 990 994 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
(A) The type I interferon response to L. pneumophila involves Ips-1 in vivo. Ips-1-/- and heterozygous littermate mice were infected intranasally with 2.5x106 LP01DeltaflaA. Bronchoalveolar lavage with PBS was performed 20 hours post infection. Type I interferon levels in the bronchoalveolar lavage fluid (BALF) were analyzed by bioassay and recombinant IFNbeta was used to determine a standard curve. A two-tailed t-test determined the differences in IFNbeta levels were statistically significant (*, p<0.01, Student's t-test) upon comparison of Ips-1+/- and Ips-1-/- mice. (B) L. pneumophila colony forming units are not significantly different in Ips-1+/- and Ips-1-/-. Bronchoalveolar lavage fluid from infected Ips-1+/- and Ips-1-/- mice was centrifuged to isolate cells. Hypotonic lysis of cells was performed and CFU were plated on buffered yeast extract charcoal plates with antibiotic selection for L. pneumophila. A two-tailed t-test determined that CFU in Ips-1+/- and Ips-1-/- mice 20 hours post infection were not statistically significantly different (ns, p>0.5, Student's t-test).
###end p 57
###begin title 58
Discussion
###end title 58
###begin p 59
###xml 236 240 236 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Stetson2">[18]</xref>
###xml 241 245 241 245 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Pichlmair1">[19]</xref>
###xml 509 531 509 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Legionella pneumophila</italic>
###xml 509 531 <span type="species:ncbi:446">Legionella pneumophila</span>
Type I interferons (IFNs) have long been appreciated as critical players in antiviral immune defense, and recent work has identified several molecular immunosurveillance pathways that induce type I IFN expression in response to viruses [18],[19]. In contrast, the roles of type I IFNs in response to bacteria, and the pathways by which bacteria induce type I IFNs, are considerably less well understood. In this study, we sought to characterize the type I IFN response to the gram-negative bacterial pathogen Legionella pneumophila. Our study focused on the type I IFN response mounted by macrophages, since this is the cell type that is believed to be the primary replicative niche in the pathogenesis of Legionnaires' Disease.
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 32 36 32 36 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Stetson1">[15]</xref>
###xml 52 66 52 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 102 105 102 105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">via</italic>
###xml 393 407 393 407 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 419 427 419 427 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 492 496 492 496 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Lippmann1">[51]</xref>
###xml 528 531 528 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dai</italic>
###xml 533 537 533 537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Zbp1</italic>
###xml 591 595 591 595 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Takaoka1">[30]</xref>
###xml 596 600 596 600 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Wang1">[31]</xref>
###xml 744 758 744 758 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 758 762 758 762 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Opitz1">[14]</xref>
###xml 842 846 842 846 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Opitz1">[14]</xref>
###xml 979 983 979 983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 988 993 988 993 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1024 1038 1024 1038 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1080 1085 1080 1085 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 1206 1213 1206 1213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 52 66 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 393 407 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 475 480 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 649 654 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 744 758 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 916 920 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1024 1038 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1219 1224 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
In agreement with previous work [15], we found that L. pneumophila induces type I IFNs in macrophages via a TLR-independent pathway that requires expression of the bacterial type IV secretion system. These results suggested that a cytosolic immunosurveillance pathway controls the IFN response in macrophages. In this report we identify the cytosolic RNA-sensing pathway as a key responder to L. pneumophila infection (Figure 1) and, in agreement with previous results using human A549 cells [51], we did not observe a role for Dai (Zbp1), a gene implicated in the response to cytosolic DNA [30],[31]. A previous study using RNA interference in the human A549 epithelial-like cell line also found a role for IPS-1 in the type I IFN response to L. pneumophila[14]. However, knockdown of RIG-I or MDA5 did not appear to affect the IFN response [14], so the role of the IPS-1 pathway was unclear. In our study, we used mice harboring targeted gene deletions to establish a role for Mda5 and Ips-1 in the type I IFN response to L. pneumophila in macrophages, and uncovered a role for Rig-i using an shRNA knockdown strategy. We also found that the cytosolic RNA-surveillance pathway regulated the IFN response in vivo in a mouse model of Legionnaires' Disease.
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 98 103 98 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 158 172 158 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 172 176 172 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 300 314 300 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 366 380 366 380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 615 619 615 619 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ablasser1">[28]</xref>
###xml 720 734 720 734 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 847 861 847 861 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 899 904 899 904 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 931 935 931 935 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-McWhirter1">[34]</xref>
###xml 937 945 937 945 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 983 997 983 997 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 158 172 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 300 314 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 366 380 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 720 734 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 847 861 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 983 997 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
After our manuscript was submitted, a report published by Chiu and colleagues also concluded that Ips-1 is required for the macrophage type I IFN response to L. pneumophila[29]. However, the report of Chiu et al differs considerably from our current work by proposing that the type I IFN response to L. pneumophila occurs via a novel and unexpected pathway in which L. pneumophila DNA reaches the host cytosol and is transcribed by RNA polymerase III to generate an RNA intermediate that is sensed by RIG-I. Others have found that the Pol III pathway can be activated by viral and AT-rich DNA in certain cell types [28]. Our data, however, are not easily reconciled with a role for the Pol III pathway in recognition of L. pneumophila. First, and perhaps most important, is the observation that the response to DNA (in contrast to the response to L. pneumophila infection) has never been seen to be Ips-1-dependent in macrophages ([34]; Figure 5). This suggests that the response to L. pneumophila is not simply a response to DNA, regardless of the mechanisms by which potentially translocated DNA might be recognized.
###end p 61
###begin p 62
###xml 35 49 35 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 173 187 173 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 345 349 345 349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ablasser1">[28]</xref>
###xml 350 354 350 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 384 398 384 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 446 451 446 451 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 496 510 496 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 567 572 567 572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 584 596 584 596 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g005">Figure 5B, E</xref>
###xml 717 722 717 722 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 762 774 762 774 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g005">Figure 5B, D</xref>
###xml 779 783 779 783 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-McWhirter1">[34]</xref>
###xml 798 803 798 803 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 876 881 876 881 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1001 1005 1001 1005 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ablasser1">[28]</xref>
###xml 1086 1091 1086 1091 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1237 1251 1237 1251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1528 1536 1528 1536 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 1642 1656 1642 1656 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 35 49 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 173 187 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 384 398 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 496 510 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1237 1251 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1642 1656 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
We considered the possibility that L. pneumophila DNA exhibits unique properties that cause it to be a particularly efficient substrate for the Pol III pathway. Indeed, the L. pneumophila genome does contain stretches of highly AT-rich DNA, and it has been reported that only highly AT-rich DNA is an efficient substrate for the Pol III pathway [28],[29]. Therefore we tested whether L. pneumophila genomic DNA, unlike other DNA, could induce an Ips-1-dependent response in macrophages. Although L. pneumophila DNA induced a robust IFN response, the response was not Ips-1-dependent (Figure 5B, E). Indeed, even the optimal Pol III substrate poly(dA-dT):poly(dA-dT) (abbreviated as pA:T) does not appear to induce an Ips-1-dependent IFN response in macrophages (Figure 5B, D and [34]). The lack of Ips-1-dependence in the response to pA:T appears to be due to an unidentified Ips-1-independent DNA-sensing pathway that recognizes pA:T and dominates over the Pol III pathway in bone marrow macrophages [28]. Thus, if translocated DNA is the relevant bacterial ligand that stimulates the Ips-1-dependent host type I IFN response, an explanation is required for how the dominant and unidentified DNA-sensing pathway is not activated. While L. pneumophila could selectively inhibit or evade the dominant DNA-sensing pathway, there is at present no evidence to support this mechanism. Moreover, in our hands, the Pol III inhibitor used by Chiu et al (ML-60218) failed to affect IFN induction or bacterial replication in macrophages (Figure 7), in contrast to what would be predicted if the Pol III pathway was selectively activated in response to L. pneumophila infection. Therefore, our data lead us to consider alternative models.
###end p 62
###begin p 63
###xml 95 109 95 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 406 420 406 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 519 533 519 533 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 543 548 543 548 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 549 560 549 560 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">independent</italic>
###xml 672 680 672 680 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 700 704 700 704 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 722 736 722 736 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 740 755 740 755 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1-dependent</italic>
###xml 830 834 830 834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ablasser1">[28]</xref>
###xml 835 839 835 839 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Chiu1">[29]</xref>
###xml 876 890 876 890 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 939 948 939 948 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g007">Figure 7B</xref>
###xml 999 1013 999 1013 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 1064 1069 1064 1069 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1096 1110 1096 1110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 95 109 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 406 420 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 519 533 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 722 736 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 876 890 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 999 1013 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1096 1110 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Although Chiu et al primarily used the RAW macrophage-like cell line in their experiments with L. pneumophila, we do not believe that cell-type-specific effects can account for the discrepancy in results. Although it is possible that RAW cells express only the Pol III pathway, this would not change the fact that the proposed model of Chiu et al invokes DNA as the primary IFN-inducing ligand produced by L. pneumophila. The simplest prediction of such a model would be that the response of bone marrow macrophages to L. pneumophila would be Ips-1-independent, as is the response of macrophages to all forms of DNA that have been tested. In contrast, as documented here (Figure 1) and by Chiu et al [29], the response to L. pneumophila is Ips-1-dependent. Moreover, 293T cells, which express only the Pol III DNA-sensing pathway [28],[29], failed to respond significantly to L. pneumophila genomic DNA, despite a robust response to pA:T (Figure 7B). Therefore, our data suggest that recognition of L. pneumophila genomic DNA by Pol III is not responsible for the Ips-1-dependent IFN response to L. pneumophila.
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 46 60 46 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 117 131 117 131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 212 226 212 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 273 279 273 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i-</italic>
###xml 325 335 325 335 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g005">Figures 5A</xref>
###xml 337 338 337 338 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g006">6</xref>
###xml 378 392 378 392 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 550 569 550 569 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Helicobacter pylori</italic>
###xml 617 621 617 621 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Rad1">[52]</xref>
###xml 673 687 673 687 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 802 816 802 816 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 951 955 951 955 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ensminger1">[53]</xref>
###xml 1302 1306 1302 1306 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Malathi1">[54]</xref>
###xml 1375 1389 1375 1389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 46 60 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 117 131 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 212 226 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 378 392 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 550 569 <span type="species:ncbi:210">Helicobacter pylori</span>
###xml 673 687 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 802 816 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 1375 1389 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
We considered two other models to explain how L. pneumophila induces a type I interferon response. The first is that L. pneumophila translocates RNA into host cells. In support of this model, we demonstrate that L. pneumophila RNA, unlike any form of DNA tested, induced a Rig-i-dependent type I IFN response in macrophages (Figures 5A, 6). However, we did not demonstrate that L. pneumophila RNA species are translocated into host cells, and this will be important to examine in future studies. Interestingly, it was recently reported that purified Helicobacter pylori RNA stimulates RIG-I in transfected 293T cells [52]. A second model to explain type I IFN induction by L. pneumophila is that infection induces a host response that indirectly results in signaling via the MDA5/RIG-I/IPS-1 pathways. L. pneumophila secretes a large number of effectors into the host cytosol and these effectors disrupt or alter a large number of host cell processes [53]. Such disruption may either lead to the generation of host-derived RNA ligands for the RIG-I and MDA5 sensors, or may result in signaling through these sensors in the absence of specific ligands. It was previously proposed that a host nuclease, RNaseL, can generate self-RNA ligands for the RIG-I and MDA5 pathways in response to viral infection [54]. Although we could not observe a role for RNaseL in the response to L. pneumophila (K.M. Monroe, unpublished data), it is conceivable that a different host enzyme can fulfill a similar function.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 136 150 136 150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 529 533 525 529 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 541 544 537 540 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Laguna1">[4]</xref>
###xml 646 650 642 646 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Seth1">[21]</xref>
###xml 949 953 945 949 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 1005 1014 1001 1010 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000665.s003">Figure S3</xref>
###xml 1096 1099 1092 1095 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Laguna1">[4]</xref>
###xml 1165 1169 1161 1165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 1246 1249 1242 1245 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Laguna1">[4]</xref>
###xml 2070 2074 2062 2066 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 2186 2194 2178 2186 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 136 150 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Our finding that a secreted bacterial effector, SdhA, previously shown to suppress host cell death, also suppresses the IFN response to L. pneumophila, is consistent with a model in which a host cell stress response leads to direct or indirect activation of the cytosolic RNA-sensing pathway. However, the mechanism by which SdhA acts on host cells remains mysterious. Laguna and colleagues provided evidence that SdhA is critical for prevention of mitochondrial disruption that occurs when host cells are infected with the DeltasdhA mutant [4]. Given that Ips-1 localizes to mitochondria and requires mitochondrial localization for its function [21], it is tempting to speculate that SdhA acts on mitochondria in a way that both prevents their disruption and interferes with the function of Ips-1. To provide evidence that SdhA acts specifically on the RIG-I/MDA5 pathway, we used transient transfections of 293T cells. SdhA repressed induction of Ifnb when co-expressed with Mda5 or Rig-I but not Trif (Figure S3). Given these results and the evidence that SdhA is translocated into host cells [4], we favor the idea that SdhA acts within host cells. Mutation of sdhA was reported not to affect translocation of other effectors into host cells [4]; thus, we tend not to support the alternative possibility that SdhA blocks translocation of the putative IFN-stimulatory ligand through the type IV secretion system. SdhA is a large protein of 1429 amino acids, but does not contain domains of known function, except for a putative coiled coil (a.a. 1037-1068). In future studies it will be important to address whether subdomains of SdhA can be identified that are required for suppression of the IFN response. It will also be important to determine whether these subdomains are distinguishable from any putative subdomains required for suppression of host cell death. In fact, our data have suggested that suppression of cell death and the IFN response may be separable functions of SdhA. We found that cell death was not required for hyperinduction of IFN by the DeltasdhA mutant, and conversely, we also found that hyperinduction of type I IFN does not lead to increased cell death (Figure 4).
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 48 52 48 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 57 62 57 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 90 104 90 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 312 316 312 316 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Fredericksen1">[47]</xref>
###xml 343 357 343 357 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 399 403 399 403 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 408 413 408 413 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 466 471 466 471 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 512 517 512 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 597 601 597 601 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 605 610 605 610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 90 104 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 343 357 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Our studies demonstrate a partial role for both Mda5 and Rig-i RNA sensors in response to L. pneumophila. Although these sensors are typically thought to respond to distinct classes of viruses, there are indications that they can also function cooperatively in response to certain stimuli, e.g., West Nile Virus [47]. Our results suggest that L. pneumophila produces ligands that can stimulate both Mda5 and Rig-i and that these two sensors cooperatively signal via Ips-1. Fitting with this model, we found that Ips-1-deficiency generally had a more severe impact on type I IFN induction than did Mda5 or Rig-i deficiency.
###end p 66
###begin p 67
###xml 123 137 123 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 206 228 206 228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Listeria monocytogenes</italic>
###xml 233 256 233 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Francisella tularensis,</italic>
###xml 286 291 286 291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 354 358 354 358 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Sun1">[25]</xref>
###xml 359 363 359 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Henry1">[43]</xref>
###xml 364 368 364 368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Crimmins1">[55]</xref>
###xml 417 425 417 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Listeria</italic>
###xml 429 440 429 440 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Francisella</italic>
###xml 572 576 572 576 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Stetson1">[15]</xref>
###xml 577 581 577 581 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ishii1">[26]</xref>
###xml 123 137 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 206 228 <span type="species:ncbi:1639">Listeria monocytogenes</span>
###xml 233 255 <span type="species:ncbi:263">Francisella tularensis</span>
Cytosolic RNA-sensing pathways are believed to respond exclusively to viral infection, and it is therefore surprising that L. pneumophila appears to trigger these pathways. Other bacterial species, such as Listeria monocytogenes and Francisella tularensis, have been shown to induce an Ips-1-independent cytosolic pathway leading to type I IFN induction [25],[43],[55]. The sensor(s) required for the IFN response to Listeria or Francisella have not yet been identified, but are widely assumed to be identical to the (also unknown) sensor(s) that respond to cytosolic DNA [15],[26].
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 0 5 0 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 9 13 9 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 37 42 37 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 123 131 123 131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 133 141 133 141 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 220 234 220 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 345 359 345 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 434 438 434 438 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Vogel1">[46]</xref>
###xml 495 509 495 509 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 548 562 548 562 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 592 597 592 597 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 642 650 642 650 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000665-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 784 789 784 789 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1006 1011 1006 1011 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 1020 1024 1020 1024 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-McWhirter1">[34]</xref>
###xml 1161 1166 1161 1166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 220 234 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 345 359 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 495 509 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 548 562 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Ips-1 or Mda5-deficiency, as well as Rig-i knockdown, did not result in a complete elimination of the type I IFN response (Figure 1, Figure 3). Thus, a cytosolic DNA-sensing pathway may also be stimulated in response to L. pneumophila infection. A minor role for a cytosolic DNA-sensing pathway would be consistent with the observation that the L. pneumophila Dot/Icm type IV secretion system can translocate DNA into recipient cells [46]. However, as discussed above, our results with purified L. pneumophila DNA suggest that cytosolic sensing of L. pneumophila DNA does not account for the Ips-1-dependent induction of IFN that we observe (Figure 5). One last possibility that we cannot eliminate is that a non-DNA, non-RNA ligand is translocated into host cells and stimulates the Ips-1 pathway. In fact, in separate work, we have found that a small bacterial cyclic dinucleotide, c-di-GMP, can trigger a type I IFN response in macrophages, but importantly, this response is entirely independent of the Ips-1 pathway [34]. Nevertheless, there may be other small molecules that can be translocated by the Dot/Icm secretion system and signal in host cells via Ips-1.
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 233 247 233 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 233 247 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Taken together, our results lead to new insights into the host immunosurveillance pathways that provide innate defense against bacterial pathogens. We demonstrate an unexpected role for a viral RNA-sensing pathway in the response to L. pneumophila, and identify a secreted bacterial effector, SdhA, that can suppress this response. Our results therefore open new possibilities for immunosurveillance of bacterial pathogens.
###end p 69

###xml 108 112 108 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 112 115 112 115 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>

###xml 121 126 121 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnar</italic>

###xml 129 133 129 133 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Muller1">[57]</xref>
###xml 135 139 135 139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Zbp1</italic>
###xml 139 142 139 142 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 142 146 142 146 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ishii2">[32]</xref>
###xml 148 158 148 158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MyD88/Trif</italic>
###xml 158 161 158 161 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 167 172 167 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Casp1</italic>
###xml 172 175 172 175 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 175 179 175 179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Li1">[58]</xref>
###xml 239 244 239 244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 244 247 244 247 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 322 327 322 327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 327 330 327 330 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 378 383 378 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 383 386 383 386 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 391 396 391 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 396 399 396 399 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 448 453 448 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 453 456 453 456 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 474 479 474 479 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 479 482 479 482 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 484 488 484 488 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Mda5</italic>
###xml 488 491 488 491 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 667 672 667 672 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MyD88</italic>
###xml 672 675 672 675 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 675 679 675 679 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Trif</italic>
###xml 679 682 679 682 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 64 69 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 190 194 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 248 252 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 466 470 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 492 496 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Bone marrow derived macrophages were derived from the following mouse strains: C57BL/6J (B6), Ips-1-/-[25], Mda5-/-[56], Ifnar-/-[57], Zbp1-/-[32], MyD88/Trif-/-, and Casp1-/-[58]. C57BL/6J mice were purchased from the Jackson Laboratory. Ips-1-/- mice were from Z. Chen (University of Texas Southwestern Medical Center). Ips-1-/- were obtained on a mixed B6/129 background and Ips-1-/- and Ips-1+/- littermate controls were generated by breeding (Ips-1-/- x B6) F1 mice to Ips-1-/-. Mda5-/- mice were from M. Colonna and S. Gilfillan (Washington University). L929-ISRE IFN reporter cells were from B. Beutler (The Scripps Research Institute). Viruses to immortalize MyD88-/-Trif-/- immortalized bone marrow derived macrophages were the generous gift of K. Fitzgerald, D. Golenbock (U. Mass, Worcester) and D. Kalvakolanu (U. Maryland). The complementation plasmid (pJB908-SdhA) was generously provided by R. Isberg (Tufts). Expression constructs pEF-BOS-RIG-I and pEF-BOS-MDA5 were generously provided by J. Jung (Harvard Medical School).
###end p 74
###begin title 75
Bacterial strains
###end title 75
###begin p 76
###xml 67 89 67 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Legionella pneumophila</italic>
###xml 112 116 108 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 130 134 122 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 139 143 127 131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhB</italic>
###xml 148 152 132 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sidH</italic>
###xml 218 222 198 202 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flaA</italic>
###xml 227 231 203 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 292 296 268 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flaA</italic>
###xml 309 313 281 285 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdhA</italic>
###xml 360 364 328 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flaA</italic>
###xml 364 368 332 336 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ren1">[12]</xref>
###xml 67 89 <span type="species:ncbi:446">Legionella pneumophila</span>
LP02 is a streptomycin-resistant thymidine auxotroph derivative of Legionella pneumophila strain LP01. LP02DeltasdhA and LP02DeltasdhADeltasdhBDeltasidH were a generous gift from R. Isberg (Tufts University). The DeltaflaADeltasdhA strain was generated by introducing an unmarked deletion of flaA in LP02DeltasdhA using the allelic exchange vector pSR47S-DeltaflaA[12].
###end p 76
###begin title 77
Cell culture
###end title 77
###begin p 78
###xml 397 402 389 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MyD88</italic>
###xml 402 405 394 397 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 405 409 397 401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Trif</italic>
###xml 409 412 401 404 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
L929-ISRE and HEK293T cells were cultured in DMEM supplemented with 10% FBS, 2 mM L-glutamine, 100 microM streptomycin, and 100 U/mL penicillin. Macrophages were derived from bone marrow cells cultured for eight days in RPMI supplemented with 10% FBS, 2 mM L-glutamine, 100 microM streptomycin, 100 U/mL penicillin, and 10% supernatant from 3T3-CSF cells, with feeding on the fifth day of growth. MyD88-/-Trif-/- immortalized macrophages were cultured in RPMI supplemented with 10% FBS, 2 mM L-glutamine, 100 microM streptomycin, and 100 U/mL penicillin.
###end p 78
###begin title 79
Reagents
###end title 79
###begin p 80
Poly I:C was from GE Biosciences, pA:T (poly(dA-dT):poly(dA-dT)) was from Sigma, and Sendai Virus was from Charles River Laboratories. Wildtype Theiler's Virus GDVII was from M. Brahic and E. Freundt (Stanford University). Pol III inhibitor (ML-60218) was from Calbiochem.
###end p 80
###begin title 81
###xml 32 46 32 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 32 46 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Isolation of nucleic acids from L. pneumophila
###end title 81
###begin p 82
Total bacterial RNA was isolated using RNAprotect Bacterial Reagent (Qiagen) and RNeasy kit (Qiagen). Genomic DNA was isolated by guanidinium thiocyanate followed by phenol:chloroform extraction. Nucleic acids were treated with RQ1 RNase-Free DNase (Promega) and/or RNaseA (Sigma).
###end p 82
###begin title 83
Quantitative RT-PCR
###end title 83
###begin p 84
###xml 64 65 64 65 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sup>
###xml 587 592 587 592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rps17</italic>
###xml 687 691 687 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb</italic>
###xml 696 722 696 722 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-ATAAGCAGCTCCAGCTCCAA-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 729 755 729 755 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-CTGTCTGCTGGTGGAGTTCA-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 763 768 763 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rps17</italic>
###xml 773 798 773 798 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-CGCCATTATCCCCAGCAAG-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 806 833 806 833 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;- TGTCGGGATCCACCTCAATG-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 841 847 841 847 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i,</italic>
###xml 851 876 851 876 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-ATTGTCGGCGTCCACAAAG-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 884 911 884 911 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-GTGCATCGTTGTATTTCCGCA-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 919 924 919 924 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ifnb,</italic>
###xml 928 954 928 954 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-AAACTCATGAGCAGTCTGCA-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 962 992 962 992 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;- AGGAGATCTTCAGTTTCGGAG G-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 1007 1029 1007 1029 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-ATCCGCCAGCGCCATA-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 1037 1064 1037 1064 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-TCAATGTGCTTCTGGGAATCC-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 594 599 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 608 613 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 681 686 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 757 762 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 835 840 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 913 918 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 994 999 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Bone marrow derived macrophages were plated at a density of 2x106 per well in 6 well plates and infected with an MOI of 1. Macrophage RNA was harvested 4 hours post infection and isolated with the RNeasy kit (Qiagen) according to the manufacturer's protocol. RNA was DNase treated with RQ1 RNase-Free DNase (Promega) and reverse transcribed with Superscript III (Invitrogen). Quantitative PCR assays were performed on the Step One Plus RT PCR System (Applied Biosystems) with Platinum Taq DNA polymerase (Invitrogen) and EvaGreen dye (Biotium). Gene expression values were normalized to Rps17 (mouse) or S9 (human) levels for each sample. The following primer sequences were used: mouse Ifnb, F, 5'-ATAAGCAGCTCCAGCTCCAA-3'and R, 5'-CTGTCTGCTGGTGGAGTTCA-3'; mouse Rps17, F, 5'-CGCCATTATCCCCAGCAAG-3' and R, 5'- TGTCGGGATCCACCTCAATG-3'; mouse Rig-i, F, 5'-ATTGTCGGCGTCCACAAAG-3' and R, 5'-GTGCATCGTTGTATTTCCGCA-3', human Ifnb, F, 5'-AAACTCATGAGCAGTCTGCA-3' and R, 5'- AGGAGATCTTCAGTTTCGGAG G-3'; human S9, F, 5'-ATCCGCCAGCGCCATA-3' and R, 5'-TCAATGTGCTTCTGGGAATCC-3'.
###end p 84
###begin title 85
Cell stimulation and transfection
###end title 85
###begin p 86
###xml 762 769 737 744 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Renilla</italic>
Cell stimulants were transfected with Lipofectamine 2000 (LF2000, Invitrogen) according to the manufacturer's protocol. Nucleic acids were mixed with LF2000 in Optimem (Invitrogen) at a ratio of 1.0 microl LF2000/microg nucleic acid and incubated for 20 minutes at room temperature. The ligand-lipid complexes were added to cells at a final concentration of 3.3 microg/ml (96-well plates) and 1.0 microg/ml (6 well plates). For poly I:C, the stock solution (2.5 mg/ml) was heated at 55degreesC for 10 minutes and cooled to room temperature immediately before mixing with LF2000. Transfection experiments were incubated for 8 hours, unless otherwise stated. RIG-I, MDA5, TRIF and SdhA expression plasmids, along with an IFNbeta-firefly luciferase reporter and TK-Renilla luciferase plasmids, were transfected with FuGENE 6 (Roche) according to the manufacturer's protocol. Nucleic acids were mixed with FuGENE 6 in Optimem at 0.5 microl/96 well and incubated for 15 minutes. Total transfected DNA was normalized to 200 ng per well using an empty pcDNA3 plasmid. Cells were stimulated 20 hours after transfection of expression plasmids.
###end p 86
###begin title 87
Type I IFN bioassay and luciferase reporter assay
###end title 87
###begin p 88
###xml 185 186 179 180 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 292 299 283 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Renilla</italic>
###xml 489 496 480 487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Renilla</italic>
###xml 522 525 513 516 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">384</sup>
###xml 652 659 643 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Renilla</italic>
Cell culture supernatants or bronchoalveolar lavage fluid (BALF) was overlayed on L929-ISRE IFN reporter cells in a 96-well plate format and incubated for 4 hours at 37degreesC and 5%CO2. L929-ISRE IFN reporter cells and HEK293T cells expressing an IFNbeta-firefly luciferase reporter and TK-Renilla luciferase were lysed in Passive Lysis Buffer (Promega) for 5 minutes at room temperature and relative light units were measured upon injection of firefly luciferin substrate (Biosynth) or Renilla substrate with the LmaxII384 luminometer (Molecular Devices). For transient transfection reporter assays, luciferase values were normalized to an internal Renilla control.
###end p 88
###begin title 89
Cytotoxicity assays
###end title 89
###begin p 90
###xml 128 132 128 132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Decker1">[59]</xref>
###xml 178 179 178 179 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sup>
###xml 234 248 234 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 316 317 316 317 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 398 402 398 402 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ren1">[12]</xref>
###xml 234 248 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
Cytotoxicity of bacterial strains was determined by measuring lactate dehydrogenase release essentially as previously described [59]. Macrophages were plated at a density of 1x105 in a 96-well plate and infected with stationary phase L. pneumophila at a multiplicity of infection (MOI) of 1. Plates were spun at 400xg for 10 minutes to allow equivalent infectivity of non-motile and motile strains [12]. Plates were re-spun 4 hours post infection and cell culture supernatants were assayed for LDH activity. Specific lysis was calculated as a percentage of detergent lysed cells.
###end p 90
###begin title 91
Growth curves
###end title 91
###begin p 92
###xml 56 60 56 60 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Coers1">[16]</xref>
###xml 126 127 126 127 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sup>
###xml 249 263 249 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 332 346 332 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 390 393 390 393 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">384</sup>
###xml 249 263 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 332 346 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 520 525 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Bacterial growth was determined as previously described [16]. Bone marrow derived macrophages were plated at a density of 1x105 per well in white 96-well plates (Nunc) and allowed to adhere overnight. Macrophages were infected with stationary-phase L. pneumophila at a multiplicity of infection (MOI) of 0.01. Growth of luminescent L. pneumophila strains was assessed by RLU with the LmaxII384 luminometer (Molecular Devices). Nonluminescent bacterial strains were analyzed for colony-forming units on buffered charcoal yeast extract plates.
###end p 92
###begin title 93
Transposon mutagenesis
###end title 93
###begin p 94
###xml 56 60 56 60 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Ren1">[12]</xref>
###xml 116 122 116 122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E.coli</italic>
###xml 147 161 142 156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">L. pneumophila</italic>
###xml 402 407 389 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MyD88</italic>
###xml 407 410 394 397 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 410 414 397 401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Trif</italic>
###xml 414 417 401 404 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 598 602 585 589 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Kwon1">[60]</xref>
###xml 116 122 <span type="species:ncbi:110766|species:ncbi:562">E.coli</span>
###xml 147 161 <span type="species:ncbi:446">L. pneumophila</span>
###xml 207 212 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Transposon mutagenesis of LP02 was previously described [12]. Briefly, the pSC123 mariner transposon was mated from E.coli SM10 lambdapir into the L. pneumophila strain LP02. Matings were plated on buffered yeast extract charcoal plates with streptomycin (100 microg/ml) and kanamycin (25 microg/ml). Single colonies were isolated and grown in overnight cultures and used to infect bone marrow derived MyD88-/-Trif-/- macrophages. After overnight incubation, levels of type I interferon in the supernatant was determined by bioassay. The site of transposon insertion was determined by Y-linker PCR [60].
###end p 94
###begin title 95
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vivo</italic>
In vivo studies
###end title 95
###begin p 96
###xml 20 25 20 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 25 28 25 28 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 44 49 44 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ips-1</italic>
###xml 49 52 49 52 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 96 97 96 97 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sup>
###xml 108 112 104 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flaA</italic>
###xml 53 57 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Age and sex-matched Ips-1-/- and littermate Ips-1+/- mice were infected intranasally with 2.5x106 LP01 DeltaflaA in 20 microl PBS. Bronchoalveolar lavage was performed 20 hours post infection via the trachea using a catheter (BD Angiocath 18 g, 1.3x48 mm) and 800 microl PBS. Type I interferon induction was determined by bioassay. Type I interferon amounts were calculated using a 4-parameter standard curve determined by dilution of recombinant IFNbeta (R&D Systems). CFUs were determined by hypotonic lysis of cells from the brochoalveolar lavage fluid (BALF). In parallel experiments, it was determined that CFU in the BALF was representative of total CFU in the lung.
###end p 96
###begin title 97
shRNA knockdown
###end title 97
###begin p 98
###xml 177 182 177 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rig-i</italic>
###xml 193 220 193 220 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-GCCCATTGAAACCAAGAAATT-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 246 274 246 274 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="gene">5&#8242;-TGACAGTGTCTTCGCTAATGAA-3&#8242;</named-content>
###xml 276 281 276 281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MyD88</italic>
###xml 281 284 281 284 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 284 288 284 288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Trif</italic>
###xml 288 291 288 291 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 393 397 393 397 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000665-Lightfield1">[10]</xref>
###xml 402 403 402 403 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
Knockdown constructs were generated with the MSCV/LTRmiR30-PIG (LMP) vector from Open Biosystems. shRNA PCR products were cloned into the LMP vector using XhoI and EcoRI sites. Rig-i sequence: 5'-GCCCATTGAAACCAAGAAATT-3', control shRNA sequence: 5'-TGACAGTGTCTTCGCTAATGAA-3'. MyD88-/-Trif-/- immortalized bone marrow derived macrophages were transduced with retrovirus as previously described [10]. GFP+ macrophages were sorted with the DAKO-Cytomation MoFlo High Speed Sorter.
###end p 98

SdhA represses MDA5 and RIG-I induction of interferon. Overexpression of SdhA in HEK293T cells results in repression of interferon induction mediated by MDA5 or RIG-I but not TRIF. (A) HEK293T cells were transfected with plasmids encoding the IFNbeta-firefly luciferase reporter, TK-Renilla luciferase reporter (for normalization), full length MDA5 and/or increasing amounts of full length SdhA. At 20 hours post transfection, cells were transfected with poly I:C and then firefly luciferase and Renilla luciferase levels were determined 8 hours later. (B) Transfection and stimulation were performed as in A, except with a RIG-I expression plasmid and/or increasing amounts of full length SdhA expression plasmid. (C) Transfection and stimulation were performed as in A, except with a Trif expression plasmid and/or SdhA.
